device eval harness** — the real-BGE golden-relevance measurement, deferred to the device session (spec in
VERIFICATION C3, fixture committed); the only reason it's here and not built is that CI can compile but never verify
it, so it rides the device.

**P-Feeds PF.3 deferrals (harvested 2026-07-06 from the PF.3 adversarial pass):** **Composite inbox PK `(paper_id, follow_id)` for per-follow provenance** — PF.3 keeps `paper_id` as the sole PK (one row per paper) + cleans inbox on unfollow; a "why is this here / which follow surfaced it" UI would justify the composite PK + a migration + a Today `GROUP BY paper_id` de-dup. Track. · **Multi-source follow badges on the arXiv grid** — generalize `CategoryWithFollowState.followed` → `Set<Source> followedOn` so the grid shows which sources a category is followed on (PF.3 keeps the grid an arXiv Boolean for minimal blast radius). · **A "Following" management surface** — one screen listing ALL non-arXiv follows grouped by source with origin-scoped unfollow (PF.3 ships only the picker; the toggle state inside it already shows what's followed per source). · **"This follow returned 0 papers recently" health hint** — a mis-mapped OpenAlex Field fails silently (HTTP 200 count=0), so a lightweight in-app signal when a follow delivers nothing over N syncs would surface misconfiguration. · **OpenAlex Subfield granularity (~250 vs 26 Fields)** — Fields keep the picker small/un-metered but may be coarse for a focused chemRxiv follow; a product decision on offering Subfield refinement. · **Per-source PDF-host allowlisting** (researchsquare.com / ssrn.com / preprints.org / osf.io) — a per-source Co-Founder decision (each needs a cookie-wall/redirect check like chemRxiv's Atypon path) to enable in-app PDF read; read-only external-open until then (`HUMAN.md` §3). · **Per-source whole-source first-sync cap** — a tighter page/window bound for SSRN-scale firehoses if the OpenAlex credit budget is ever pressured (the page-1 short-circuit already bounds the common case).

**P-Reader2 device-verification UX harvest (2026-07-15, emulator session — refinements the on-device pass surfaced; most are small, all reversible):** _(**Phase P-RPolish** draws PP.1–PP.4 from this list — theme cycle, jump precision, zoom-reset, matte, and the a11y CDs are **in scope**; ink-polarity matte, zoom coach-mark, toolbar overflow, night-toggle snackbar, and the appearance sheet stay **backlog**.)_ **Jump-to-page precision** — the Slider is continuous over 1..pageCount, so on a 50+-page PDF one pixel ≈ several pages and hitting an exact page is near-impossible; add a numeric text field and/or +/- steppers beside the slider (observed: a single tap jumped 9→16). **→ in PP.2 (numeric field + steppers).** · **In-reader path back to SYSTEM theme** — the reader toolbar toggle only ever writes explicit LIGHT/DARK, so once tapped a user can't restore "follow the OS" from inside the reader (only Settings); consider a 3-state cycle or long-press-for-SYSTEM. · **Soften the dark-mode matte** — the transparent-figure card is a hard `#ffffff` (reader.css) which can halo/jar against the soft-dark body; try a near-white or a hairline border + tuned padding. · **Matte ink-polarity edge case** — `ImageAlpha` detects transparency but not ink luminance, so a transparent figure drawn in WHITE/light ink becomes invisible on the white matte (the inverse of the bug being fixed); a dominant-ink-luminance check could pick a dark matte for light-ink figures. · **Zoom discoverability** — pinch + double-tap are wholly hidden gestures with no on-screen cue; a one-time hint or an explicit zoom affordance would help first-time users. · **Reset zoom on deliberate navigation** — zoom is `remember`-only and does NOT reset on a jump-to-page (only on reopen/rotation), so jumping while zoomed can land in a panned/awkward state; reset to 1× on a deliberate jump. · **HTML reader toolbar crowding** — 5 action icons (Search/TOC/Ask/Night/PDF) + title + back on a Pixel_3a width risks sub-48dp targets; consider an overflow menu on narrow screens. · **Global night-toggle feedback** — the reader toggle silently changes every reader app-wide; a subtle snackbar ("Applied to all readers") would make the scope legible. · **Reader a11y content-descriptions** — the page pill's `content-desc` is just "Jump to page" (drops the live "N / M") and the night toggle never announces on/off state; merge state into both for TalkBack. · **Reader-local appearance sheet** (expansion) — the reader offers only night-mode; a lightweight in-reader text-size / serif / line-height sheet (the CSS already defines `.ltx_font_serif/sansserif`) would serve readers who don't want to change the whole-OS font scale.

**PDF-zoom-blank hotfix deferrals (harvested 2026-07-16):** **Byte-bounded LRU bitmap cache — ✓ RESOLVED 2026-07-16 (`PdfPageCache`).** Shipped a single-owner cache bounded by a **total-byte budget** (`maxMemory/6`, not a fixed count → no foldable OOM), recycling only **off-window** pages (a composed page is `pin`ned → never the permanent-spinner or use-after-free case), with **single-flight** per-index renders and scroll-back **reuse** (a revisited page is a cache hit, not a re-render). `PdfPageCacheTest` covers eviction/pin-safety/MRU-protection/single-flight. Researched first: `androidx.pdf` (Jetpack) is SDK-35-only + Fragment-based → not viable; `PdfRenderer` requires ARGB_8888 (no RGB_565 memory halving); the byte-`LruCache` sizing convention is the canonical pattern. · **Crisper zoom → promoted to the captured-vision Phase P-ReaderZoom below** (was: re-rasterise the focal region at `scale·targetWidth`). · **Zoom discoverability** — pinch/double-tap are still uncued (already in the PR.UX harvest above).

**P-HTML PH.5 deferrals (harvested 2026-06-27, in-vision but out-of-PH.5):** **Figure-refresh affordance** — a paper first opened offline (or past the deadline) bakes figcaption placeholders into the stored body; a later online re-open hits the `.complete` cache and won't auto-upgrade. **Re-deferred out of PH.6 (2026-07-04, recorded):** not chrome-only work — it needs a cache-bypass `load(force)` mode + a keep-cached-body-on-failed-refetch state machine (offline re-open is the canonical trigger; blanking a readable cached paper is unacceptable) + a snackbar surface + an `ltx_placeholder` probe with a known false-positive class (over-cap/unresolvable figures). Natural home: a small standalone reader-chrome PR after PH.6 — now strictly cheaper (the restore survives its reload; the `.position` sidecar survives the re-store); its lying "download to view" placeholder copy was reworded in PH.6. (Was: manual "refresh figures" action in PH.6's reader chrome) · **True foreground-priority rate limiter** — `ArxivRateLimiter` is plain FIFO; a figure-heavy open roughly doubles a concurrent FollowSync's wait. A preemptive/priority limiter (or a separate low-priority image lane) would remove the bounded starvation PH.5 only caps · **Honor native arxiv.org `Crawl-delay: 15`** for image sub-resources specifically (PH.5 uses the global 3s; revisit if arXiv signals image-fetch pressure) · **Inline-SVG / vector figures** — LaTeXML can emit inline `<svg>` or `.svg`/vector figures; PH.5's raster path rejects non-raster `Content-Type` to figcaption. Route vector figures through `SvgSanitizer` (→ PH.8) · **Blank-slot CLS polish** — phase-1 shows a brief figcaption-placeholder flash before figures inline; a sized empty slot (width/height aspect-ratio) would remove the flash/shift · **Streaming/encode-as-you-go inlining** to shave the triple-hold peak memory (raw bytes + base64 + assembled body) on very large papers.

**P-Tools PT.1 deferrals (harvested 2026-07-05):** **Fully library-scoped DAO search** — `search_my_library` searches a wide candidate pool (200/leg) over the whole cached `papers` corpus then filters to the library before fusion (the post-diff-review F1 fix); for a *very large* browsed corpus a relevant library paper could theoretically rank past the 200-candidate cutoff. A library-predicate FTS query + a library-restricted vector scan would make it exact; adopt if device use shows misses. · **Option A citation re-sourcing** (suppress pre-turn RAG when the tool is on + mint `[n]` citations from tool results) — needs a mid-loop citation channel across the `Flow<ChatChunk>` boundary + a numbering-ownership move; PT.1 shipped Option B (keep RAG, prose `arXiv:<id>` for tool hits). · **PT.2 external-tools consent gate** — PT.1's `tools_enabled` currently gates the *library* tool ("Search my library"); PT.2's external tools (arXiv/S2/chemRxiv, which query third parties) need their own gate/consent, distinct from library search (a user may want library-yes, web-no). Decide in PT.2. **✓ RESOLVED (PT.2, 2026-07-05):** a NEW `web_search_enabled` column (`MIGRATION_5_6`) + `ToolConsent(library, external)`; `tools_enabled` stays the library gate (anti-repurpose ruling). · **"Search my library" default ON vs OFF** — shipped OFF (privacy-first); a one-line flip if the Co-Founder prefers opt-out (HUMAN.md §1). · **Live tool-arg streaming already in the phase deferrals**; PT.1's activity bubble is buffered-to-complete.

Cut from PT.3 because none has an MVP caller (import routes through the arXiv `getPaper`, not S2 details) and recommendations uses a different `/recommendations/v1` path prefix + envelope. Each is one client method + one `ToolSpec` row + tests when demanded — no seam-shape change; `search_semantic_scholar` already ships the S2 surface. · **`CitationSyncWorker` spacing integration test** — the client move left the worker byte-untouched and spacing is internal to the client's 1.2s mutex (covered by the shipped citation-sync path + the client's own tests), so a full WorkManager spacing test was judged low-value vs. its harness cost; add if the worker is ever modified. · **Non-arXiv (S2/generic) import** — unchanged `HUMAN.md` §3 carve-out (needs a generic-id schema decision — Co-Founder steer); PT.3 imports only arXiv-resolvable hits (`importable` flag), search surfaces the rest read-only.

**P-Tools PT.4 deferrals (harvested 2026-07-05):** **chemRxiv `/categories` + `/items/{id}` + `/items/doi/{doi}` detail endpoints** — one client method + one `ToolSpec` each when demanded (mirrors the S2 details/batch/recommendations deferral); MVP is `search_chemrxiv` (`term`/`limit`/`skip`) only. · **chemRxiv `author`/`searchDateFrom-To`/`categoryIds` search filters** → backlog (MVP is free-text `term`). · **`MAX_CHEM_RESULTS` bump 25→50** if a live-capture proves the API accepts 50 (kept 25 = house convention, always API-safe; a trivial one-const change). · **Generic (non-arXiv/DOI-keyed) import of chemRxiv results** — reinforces the OPEN `HUMAN.md` §3 carve-out (natural home: a future source-abstraction phase, not P-Tools); PT.4 shipped chemRxiv read-only by design. · **Live-GET envelope confirmation** — the chemRxiv wire is DTO-grounded against a real wrapper's parse but not a live GET (CI is Cloudflare-gated); rides `VERIFICATION.md` §Q-PT11 (a renamed field degrades to empty-not-crash).

**Test-infra flake (harvested 2026-07-05):** a **nondeterministic cross-test coroutine-leak** in the `:app` unit suite surfaces as `UncaughtExceptionsBeforeTest` at whatever test runs next in order (seen at `FilteredPapersViewModelTest` in PT.2, `ChatRepositoryTest` in PT.3 — always passes in isolation + on re-run). A ViewModel test leaks a `viewModelScope` job that throws after its `runTest` block closes. Not a product defect and it never blocks a green re-run, but it can cause a spurious CI red (→ re-kick). Fix: audit the `AskViewModel`/settings VM tests for an undrained launched coroutine (likely a fire-and-forget `viewModelScope.launch` not awaited by `advanceUntilIdle`), or add a `Dispatchers.resetMain`-ordering guard. Standalone test-hygiene PR.

**P-Tools PT.2 deferrals (harvested 2026-07-05):** **Concurrent tool execution** (already in the phase deferrals above) — PT.2 serializes tool calls through the one FIFO arXiv limiter; a 5-round uncached turn is ~12–15s of enforced spacing (bounded by `max_results≤25` + 320-char snippets + 4000-char clip). A bounded-concurrent, per-host-mutex-respecting executor is a latency optimization, not a correctness gap; adopt if device use shows the serial wait is objectionable. · **`import_to_library` already-in-library disclosure nuance (accepted)** — the activity bubble tiers on `(egress, toolName)` at draft granularity, so a re-import of an already-saved paper (a purely LOCAL `isInLibrary` check, no fetch) still renders the external "Imported to library (left your device)" label. This is **over**-disclosure (safe direction — never claims local for an egress); making it exact needs a result-granular draft field. Recorded, not built. · **Deck chip flipped during an open confirm** — does not change the already-frozen `pendingConfirm` turn (the confirm honestly shows the tool set captured at `prepare()`); the flip applies to the next send. Documented behavior, not a data gap.

**P-Dispatch deferrals (harvested 2026-07-07):** **`deep_dive` routine-template softening** — the Deep-Dive Analyst starter preamble (`RoutineTemplates.kt`) still says "fetch the PDF … never work from the abstract alone"; soften it for a non-arXiv paper whose PDF is un-fetchable. Deferred: it's *future-setup-only* (existing routines keep their pasted text), already covered at dispatch time by the per-paper `pdf_fetchable` flag + the envelope prose, and changing it forces a `CATALOG_VERSION` bump + catalog-golden update — disproportionate now. · **`pdf_fetchable` host-reachability refinement** — the flag is currently the conservative `ref is ArxivRef` (bioRxiv/medRxiv PDFs are actually open but reported unfetchable); a per-host rule (bio/med `full.pdf` = fetchable, chemRxiv Atypon = not) would tighten it (the field is already optional — no schema change to refine later). · **`published`/`updated` canonical form** — the code emits a full ISO-8601 instant; the §4 example now matches (self-healed), but whether date-only was ever the intended contract is unresolved. · **Non-arXiv multi-select dispatch on device** — the un-gate covers the detail-screen send + the single `buildPayload` chokepoint every multi-select path routes through; confirm on device that Library/Filtered/Explore multi-select also surface it.

**P-OA deferrals (harvested 2026-07-16 from the resolver workflow + adversarial passes — routed, not dropped):** **Durable `oa_resolutions` cache** (Room table keyed by `storage_id`, TTL-backed) — v1 memoizes only for the VM lifetime, so re-opening the same paper re-bills one call (red-line-compliant: each call is behind an explicit tap). The persistent table is the **enabler** for the three items below and is deferred because it is a schema change with its own migration + test. · **Explore result-list "published version available" badge / OA card chip** — feasible ONLY by reading the durable cache; MUST NEVER resolve at list render or scroll (hard metering rule) — record that constraint with the item. · **Zero-tap re-reveal** of a cached-found OA button on detail re-open (depends on the cache). · **"Save the published version to library"** (attach the published DOI / persist the VoR as its own entry — touches the library dedup model). · **PDF-viewer error-state placement** of the OA action — the detail-screen gate `!isPdfFetchable()` is always false where the PDF viewer is reachable (IN_APP sources), and the user is usually offline in that error state (resolve would also fail → error-on-error); needs its own gate + connectivity precheck. · **bioRxiv/medRxiv (IN_APP) + arXiv published-VoR surfacing** — v1 gates to browser-tier (the actual gap); an IN_APP paper that was also journal-published could offer its VoR as a distinct secondary action (needs a 3-action hierarchy design + echo-suppression). · **Extend the shared `normalizeDoi` to strip a `/vN` tail (RS slash-versioned DOIs) + a migration to recompute `doi_norm`** — the resolver uses a *local* `baseDoiKey` today to avoid desyncing the stored key; making the shared de-dup key handle RS `/vN` is a real latent improvement but needs a `doi_norm` backfill migration + tests (its own subphase, mirrors the v11→v12 `.vN` work). · **Multiple OA candidates affordance** (PMC + publisher) — v1 picks the single best `publishedVersion` PDF; an "other free sources" menu is later. · **Confirm the OpenAlex `mailto` is a fixed app contact, not the user's email** — the new per-opened-paper trigger correlates "this user opened this exact paper" with whatever identity `mailto` carries (pre-existing property of every OpenAlex call, not new to this feature; `api_key` is already redacted from surfaced errors). Verify at the `AppModule` binding; if it is the user's address, move to a generic polite-pool contact (`HUMAN.md` §1 (P-OA, 2026-07-16)).

| 2026-07-16 | **P-Ambient PA.2 shipped — the "Likely relevant" home-screen Glance widget** (resuming the ACTIVE P-Ambient phase after the reader/P-OA work leapfrogged it; loop "top-to-bottom, next open task"). Surfaces the P5 calibrated top-k likely-relevant papers on the home screen, calmly and locally (titles/count never leave the device). Adopted **Glance 1.1.1** (`glance-appwidget` + `glance-material3`) — the Co-Founder pre-approved the dep 2026-07-12; researched-confirmed the alternative (Jetpack `androidx.pdf`… n/a; the Compose-native Glance is the path). **Key calls:** the app's first `@EntryPoint` (`WidgetEntryPoint` via `EntryPointAccessors.fromApplication`) so the system-instantiated receiver reaches the `@Singleton` DAOs; a new `InboxDao.activeInboxTopK(cut, k)` reusing the SHARED `RelevanceThreshold.cut` (no drift with digest/Today) but dropping `digested_at IS NULL` + the recency floor (a widget shows *current best*, not a one-shot "new" alert) while keeping `score IS NOT NULL` (cold-start never fakes relevance); refresh piggybacks `EmbeddingWorker`'s scoring pass via `updateAll` (zero extra wakeups, `runCatching`); a new `MainActivity.EXTRA_PAPER_STORAGE_ID` deep-link so a tap opens the exact paper for **any** origin (not just the arXiv VIEW path) — the row action is Glance's reified **`actionStartActivity<MainActivity>(actionParametersOf(…))`**, deliberately **not** the raw-`Intent` overload: emulator testing this session proved Glance's raw-`Intent` `actionStartActivity(Intent)` **drops both the data URI and the extras through its cold-start trampoline** (onCreate saw `data=null extras=null` → the row deep-link silently no-op'd to Today), whereas `ActionParameters` survive because Glance serializes them through its own action pipeline (delivered verbatim as the `EXTRA_PAPER_STORAGE_ID` extra on cold start). `GlanceTheme` reuses the app `LightColors`/`DarkColors` (now `internal`) via `ColorProviders` (Glance can't run M3 dynamic colour). **Placing the widget IS the opt-in** (no toggle); **read-only → no migration**. Ethos held: no new egress, no telemetry, empty when cold-start (silence over noise). `InboxDaoTest.activeInboxTopK` covers the query; green `./gradlew build`. **Emulator-verified end-to-end** (Pixel API 34, debug): placed via the launcher picker (3×2 preview + description), rendered the header + real calibrated top-6 rows, a **cold-start row tap opened the exact paper detail** and the header opened Today. Residual for a real device (dark-theme render, non-arXiv row, worker refresh, airplane resilience) → VERIFICATION §PA. |
| 2026-07-16 | **`PdfPageCache` shipped — a byte-bounded LRU page-bitmap cache (Co-Founder-directed follow-up to the pinch-blank fix; "do it thoroughly").** The pinch-blank fix deleted an eager per-item `bitmap.recycle()` and left bitmap lifetime to GC; this restores a *safe* memory bound + adds scroll-back reuse. **Researched first** (web): `androidx.pdf` (Jetpack) is `1.0.0-alpha01`, **SDK-35-only + Fragment-based** → not viable for minSdk-26/Compose (watch); `PdfRenderer` **requires ARGB_8888** (no RGB_565 memory halving); the canonical robust pattern is a **byte-sized `LruCache`** (`byteCount`, ~1/8 heap) recycling an evicted bitmap only when certainly unused. **Design** (every adversarial trap designed out): single owner, bounded by **total bytes** (`maxMemory/6`, not a fixed count → no foldable OOM); recycle **only off-window** pages (a composed page is `pin`ned via a DisposableEffect → never the use-after-free or permanent-spinner case; a freshly-rendered page is MRU → protected during the pin-commit window); **single-flight** per index (a fast scroll can't double-render or leak the loser); a revisited page is a **hit** (no re-render). All map/accounting under a fast non-suspending monitor; the render runs outside the lock (PdfRenderer self-serialises). P-Read invariants byte-identical (item heights/scrollFraction/scrollToItem/persist untouched). `PdfPageCacheTest` (7 cases: hit-reuse, byte-budget eviction, pin-never-evicted, MRU-protection, unpin-trims, evictAll-recycles, single-flight). Green `./gradlew build`. **Crisp-zoom vision → captured as future Phase P-ReaderZoom** (tiled region-render at zoom resolution). Device-verify (fast-scroll memory on a large PDF) → VERIFICATION §PDF-ZOOM. |
| 2026-07-16 | **Reader hotfix — PDF pinch-zoom no longer blanks the page (Co-Founder device report).** On a real Samsung, the second/third pinch turned the in-app PDF page BLANK (pill still updating, no spinner). Root-caused via an Ultracode workflow (root-cause hunt + minimal-vs-redesign designs + adversarial synthesis) + my own file:line validation to TWO interacting bugs in `PdfViewerScreen.kt`: (1) `val zoomed = PdfZoom.isZoomed(scale)` read `scale` **directly in the composition scope**, so the "draw-only" zoom actually recomposed the whole `LazyColumn` on every pinch frame (the `graphicsLayer{}` lambda correctly defers its reads; this one line leaked the subscription); (2) the PR.UX.2 eager `bitmap.recycle()` in `PdfPage`'s `onDispose` then **raced** — the per-frame churn disposed a boundary item and recycled its bitmap while the scaled `graphicsLayer`'s retained draw still referenced it → a recycled bitmap paints blank (no spinner because `bitmap` is non-null, just recycled). Pinch-only + not-emulator-reproducible fits exactly (adb can't pinch; double-tap's single scale write doesn't trigger the churn). **Fix** (adversarial-recommended minimal synthesis; P-Read scroll invariants byte-identical): `zoomed` now reads through `derivedStateOf` (recomposes only on the zoom/not-zoom boolean flip, not per frame) → kills the churn; the racy per-item `recycle()` is **deleted** (bitmap lifetime → GC, bounded by the composed window + the heap-capped render width) → no bitmap can be recycled mid-draw; plus a recycled-bitmap draw guard. **A `clip=true` "polish" was tried and REVERTED** — on-device (double-tap zoom + theme-toggle-while-zoomed) it forced an offscreen buffer that re-recorded BLANK on a recomposition-while-zoomed (a regression the emulator smoke caught before merge; without it the same recomposition renders fine). **Rejected the heavier per-page-zoom redesign** (silently changes zoom to non-continuous, leans on unreliable `zIndex`, needs its own cache). Deferred → backlog: a byte-bounded LRU bitmap cache (only if fast-scroll heap pressure shows on device) + crisper re-render at zoom scale. Device-verify (real pinch) → VERIFICATION §PDF-ZOOM; the recycle-deletion memory tradeoff logged HUMAN §1. |
| 2026-07-16 | **Phase P-OA shipped — the OA published-version resolver (browser-open tier).** The v2.2.0 device report (an RS "seed" preprint with no PDF, only a link to its free Wiley VoR) becomes a **"Find free PDF"** detail action: one host-free OpenAlex title search (`sourceId=null`) → a pure three-tier picker (`OaFulltextResolver`) → a browser-open of the published OA PDF. **Planned via an Ultracode workflow** (2 resolver designs + UX + a 3-lens adversarial stress pass, 6 Opus agents) + my own file:line validation + **live `api.openalex.org` verification** (the RS work is genuinely *unmerged* — its `locations[]` carries only Research Square — so a crosswalk is *required*, not a `get-by-DOI`; the title search cleanly returns the Wiley `article` [type/version/first-author separable] alongside the preprint). **Adversarial findings folded in (the ceremony earned it):** retraction/erratum **hard-reject** (the single worst outcome — neither original design caught it); a **typed `OaResult{Found/None/Error}`** replacing a `String?` (fixes offline-as-false-None AND a Tier-C own-PDF mislabeled "published"); order-sensitive Levenshtein + **first-author-only** surname (kills the coverage design's order-insensitive-Jaccard / author-anywhere false positive); an **author-less strict-title path** so the feature isn't dead for author-stripped SSRN/RS; arXiv/BROWSER metering gate; `withContext(default)` off-main + length-capped Levenshtein; `withTimeout`; provenance-below-row (no reflow); "None" as a caption not a dead disabled chip. **Personal-validation call that improved on the delegated fix:** the agent proposed extending the shared `normalizeDoi` to strip RS `/vN` — but `doi_norm` is a *stored, indexed* column, so that desyncs existing rows (fork regression) without a migration; used a **resolver-local `baseDoiKey`** instead (zero DB blast radius) and routed the shared-key extension to the backlog. **Zero schema change, zero new egress host, one OpenAlex call per explicit tap.** Deferrals (durable cache + list badge + save-VoR + PDF-error placement + bio/med/arXiv VoR + shared-`/vN` migration + `mailto` check) routed to the backlog + `HUMAN.md` §1 (P-OA, 2026-07-16). | 2026-07-10 | **PE.1b shipped — PsyArXiv actually delivers papers now; and I caught myself propagating an unverified claim.** `OpenAlexBackend.toHit` did `bareDoi() ?: return null`, but PsyArXiv is OSF-hosted and **99.4% DOI-null on the recent window a follow actually syncs (340 of 342 works)** — so following it silently discarded nearly everything, and PFP.3's health hint would then have blamed the *feed* for the *app's* drop. **Fix:** `PreprintHit.nativeId` is now the identity (DOI when the source has one, else the OpenAlex work id `W…`), `doi` became nullable, and the intra-page dedup key falls back to `nativeId` — a `normalizeDoi(doi) ?: doi` key would have collapsed every DOI-less hit onto one bucket and delivered a single paper. Additive **v12→v13** adds `papers.landing_url`: an OSF paper has neither DOI nor PDF, so before this its `canonicalUrl()` resolved to the **empty string** — no link at all. **Self-heal:** my own PE.1b note (taken from an agent probe) claimed PsyArXiv's `publication_date` is a re-harvest artifact needing `from_created_date`. I verified directly: **both halves are false** — `from_publication_date:2026-06-26` returns 342 works, and `from_created_date` is not a valid OpenAlex filter (the API errors). Acting on it would have broken PsyArXiv outright. Corrected here and in the `openalex-api-contract` memory, which now records the debunked claim so it can't be re-adopted. Tests: `Migration12To13Test`, two `FollowSyncWorkerTest` cases (DOI-less hit ingested under its work id; three DOI-less hits stay distinct), two `PaperTest` canonicalUrl cases. Green `./gradlew build`. **Next: PE.3 (multi-source search).** |
| 2026-07-10 | **PE.2 shipped — the de-dup key finally matches on both sides, and the import path stops forking.** Two shipped bugs, one additive migration (**v11→v12**). (1) **`paperIdByDoi` matched the RAW `doi` column while every caller passed `normalizeDoi(...)`** — so a versioned chemRxiv DOI (`…7234721.v5`) was stored one way and queried another and silently never de-duped. Added `papers.doi_norm` as the *match key* (leaving `doi` as the verbatim citeable value), re-pointed the index at it, dropped the now-dead `index_papers_doi` (`paperIdByDoi` was its sole consumer). The key is written through the single `Paper.toEntity()` chokepoint, so a stored row's key is by construction exactly what the query passes. **Ruling: the backfill runs in Kotlin, not SQL** — SQLite has no `REGEXP`, so a pure-SQL backfill could lowercase but never strip `.vN`, leaving precisely the rows this migration exists to fix still broken; reusing `normalizeDoi` guarantees back-filled keys are byte-identical to future writes. Rows are collected before updating (never mutate a table while walking its cursor). (2) **`saveExternalPaper` forked a cross-posted paper** — it passed `arxivId=null` and never consulted `paperIdByDoi`, so PFP.1's de-dup covered the *follow* path but not the *import* path (reachable from the chat `import_to_library` tool). It now reuses an existing same-DOI row (arXiv-origin preferred) and deliberately does **not** overwrite it — an import's metadata is thinner, so clobbering a richer native row would regress (the PFP.1 degraded-metadata lesson). Also corrected a self-reassuring comment there that claimed "chemRxiv never does" carry an arXiv cross-id — measured 0.0097%. Tests: `Migration11To12Test` (identity-hash, `.vN` backfill, two-rows-share-a-key anti-brick), new `PaperRepositoryTest` ×3, a `FollowSyncWorkerTest` versioned-DOI regression. Green `./gradlew build`. **Next: PE.1b (PsyArXiv identity) then PE.3 (multi-source search).** |
| 2026-07-10 | **PE.1 shipped — the curated vocabularies are now MEASURED, and the measurement overturned every intuitive subset.** Ran a live `group_by=primary_topic.field.id` census of each OpenAlex source (2024+ works) rather than reasoning from source names. Adopted an objective rule — **offer a Field iff it carries ≥1% of the source's recent works** — and render curated lists in **descending real mass**. **Three corrections the data forced:** (1) chemRxiv's "chemistry-adjacent" nine omitted **Computer Science (4.68%)** and **Medicine (3.85%)** — comp-chem and med-chem are real, not noise; 11 Fields → 95.9%. (2) PsyArXiv's obvious {Psychology, Neuroscience, Social Sciences} omitted **Medicine at 9.04%** (clinical psych/psychiatry). (3) **SSRN was badly wrong**: the intuitive {Econ, Business, Social, Decision} covers only **27.9%** of recent works and omits **Engineering — SSRN's #1 recent Field at 21.87%**. Post-Elsevier "Preprints with SSRN" turned it into a broad STEM firehose; the law/finance mental model holds only all-time. The Co-Founder's "megajournals keep all 26" call was **confirmed** empirically (Research Square + Preprints.org: top-10 covers just 80–84%, every Field >0.15% — a subset would hide content, not noise). The device-reported junk is confirmed noise: chemRxiv Dentistry **0.04%**, Arts & Humanities **0.10%**, Veterinary **0.02%**. A bad Field id now fails **loud** at build instead of degrading to a silently-empty follow. **Two bugs surfaced by the same census** → `PE.1b` (PsyArXiv 98.97% DOI-null is discarded at ingest) and the correction below. |
| 2026-07-10 | **CORRECTION to the PFP.1 record — the arXiv-crosswalk premise was true but is empirically near-inert.** The PFP.1 row below calls the OpenAlex `locations[]` arXiv cross-id "load-bearing" and says DOI-only de-dup "would ship this as a no-op". **Measured 2026-07-10: only 6 of 61,795 chemRxiv-primary works (0.0097%) carry an arXiv `locations[]` entry.** The memory `openalex-api-contract.md` was *correct* that such a work **can** exist — it is not refuted — but the inference that the crosswalk carries the de-dup is wrong: it fires roughly once in ten thousand. OpenAlex keeps a cross-post as **two separate works with different DOIs** (`10.48550/arXiv.*` vs `10.26434/chemrxiv-*`), so neither the crosswalk *nor* DOI-matching catches the common arXiv↔chemRxiv cross-post; real coverage would need title normalization. **PFP.1's code is still correct and cheap** — the crosswalk is the right mechanism and fires when it fires; only the *claimed impact* was overstated. Recording the number so a future session doesn't over-weight it. Title-normalized de-dup → backlog. |
| 2026-07-07 | **CHECKPOINT P-FeedPolish ticked — Phase P-FeedPolish complete (PFP.1 de-dup + PFP.2 manage screen + PFP.3 health hint).** Full `./gradlew build` green on merged `main`; both new migrations identity-hash-tested and `10.json`/`11.json` committed (no destructive migration in the phase). **Red-line audit green:** the manage screen is pure-DB (ViewModel depends only on `CategoryRepository`) → zero-network-on-open holds structurally; the phase added **no new egress host**; the arXiv ≥3s / OpenAlex ~1.2s limiters were untouched; no `:core:*→:app` import leak; no telemetry. **The audit earned its keep:** it caught that the deferred **multi-source-badges (item-3)** decision — which the PFP.1 row claimed was routed to HUMAN.md — was in fact only in the ROADMAP backlog; added the product-call row to HUMAN.md §3 (vacuous-as-specced: arXiv grid codes and non-arXiv follow values are disjoint vocabularies; a real cross-source badge needs a discipline crosswalk that doesn't exist; the PFP.2 manage screen already meets the underlying need). | 2026-07-07 | **PFP.3 shipped — follow health hint (the last P-FeedPolish build subphase).** A soft "No new papers recently" subtitle appears on the manage screen for a follow whose recent syncs delivered nothing. **Migration v10→v11** adds `follows.empty_sync_streak` (additive `INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0`; `MIGRATION_7_8` idiom + a numeric-default with no quote-normalization hazard — oracle `chat_sessions.web_search_enabled`). **Load-bearing correctness:** `FollowSyncWorker.syncFollow` now returns a three-way **`SyncResult {Fetched(count)|Failed|Skipped}`** instead of a `Boolean`, so a *fetch failure* (`Failed` → retry, cursor frozen) can never inflate the streak — only a real `Fetched(0)` bumps it via the count-aware atomic `markSynced(id, syncedAt, delivered)` (CASE 0→+1 else→reset). `Skipped` (bad origin) freezes both cursor and streak. Count = `fresh.size` **pre-inbox-IGNORE**, so a working-but-redundant follow resets rather than reading as dead. **Planned via an Ultracode Workflow** (10 agents: map → 3 designs → 3 adversarial stress → completeness critic → synthesis); my **personal validation** confirmed the load-bearing claims at file:line (`markSynced` has exactly 1 caller + 0 test callers → safe signature change; `syncFollow`'s Boolean consumed only by `doWork`; the numeric-defaultValue byte-match oracle; the backup path maps `BackupFollow` explicitly so the new column is never serialized → a restored follow's streak resets, correct). **Deviation adopted (documented):** `EMPTY_STREAK_WARN = 4`, not the planned 3 — the streak counts sync *events* not wall-clock and `syncNow` injects extra events, so 3 (≈18h at 6h cadence) false-positives on niche-feed lulls; 4 (≈24h) clears a quiet day; the time-agnostic soft copy makes a residual FP harmless. Green `./gradlew build`. **Deferred → backlog:** OpenAlex `meta.count` sharper mis-map signal; a `last_delivered_at` wall-clock signal; streak-reset-on-re-enable (no disable toggle exists yet). **Next: CHECKPOINT P-FeedPolish.** |

| 2026-07-06 | **P4.1 shipped — the two-sided scorer is now live + follows cold-start.** `EmbeddingWorker.scoreInbox` is replaced by a delegated call to a new injectable **`InboxScorer`** — a genuinely better seam (adopted directly per the "choose the better design" directive): the ranking logic is now unit-testable against real Room DAOs without standing up the embedding/download pipeline (the worker's other deps: `embeddingService`/`modelDownloader`/`vectorIndex`/`ragIndexer`). `InboxScorer` builds positive centroids (library saves ∪ thumbs-up) and a pooled negative centroid (dismisses ∪ thumbs-down from `paper_feedback`), **dedupes** (a positive is never a negative), **model-guards** every vector read (a stale-model/wrong-dim embedding is skipped, not crashed on `dot()`), and seeds cold-start from `InboxDao.activeIdsFromEnabledFollows` (enabled-follow join, minus dislikes) *before* the <10 gate — so a follows-only user gets ranking instead of recency, while a truly empty profile still falls back to recency. `InboxRepository.dismiss()` now snapshots a durable negative into `paper_feedback`; a new **`undoDismiss`** clears it (personal-pass catch: an undone dismiss must be complete — the VM `undo` routes DISMISSED→`undoDismiss`, SAVED→the existing unsave+restore). | 2026-07-04 | **P-HTML PH.6 shipped — TOC + anchor nav + reading-position persistence (the judges’ hybrid, personally validated).** The planning pass produced three stances (minimal-sidecar / robust-anchor-position / Room-first-class); the lifecycle + UX judges independently killed any ratio-based payload (**the PH.5 phase-2 reload fires 5–30 s into every first online read and inflates content height above the reading point — a ratio is mathematically guaranteed to land in the wrong paragraph**), and the scope judge’s complexity objection was paid for by re-deferring figure-refresh. **Decisions:** anchor+offset payload over ratio (fraction floor for anchor-less papers) · `.position` **sidecar over Room/DataStore** (no migration for one row per paper; a verified FK wart — the reader opens papers with no `papers` row — makes a CASCADE FK actively wrong; Room recorded as the trigger-gated upgrade) · **ModalBottomSheet over the row’s "Compose drawer"** (zero drawer precedent in the app; a sheet overlays in its own window so open/close never reloads the WebView) · **single-slot arbitration** (a jump holds through a settle window; probes demote after; restore only ever reads) · **generation-stamped** probe/restore callbacks (every race in all three designs traced to acting on a stale document) · restores instant, taps animate · conceal-reveal reload · the probe is the app’s FIRST ValueCallback data return — treated as hostile (validate the anchor against `doc.anchors`, clamp, never render; SPEC §12). **My validation:** confirmed every file:line claim on merged code; resolved the appendix-id checkpoint (no `A*` ids in any fixture → backlog, no regex change); added the update-block reload guard, defensive `mkdirs`, and factory-time tick suppression the blueprint under-specified; caught the test-harness virtual-clock trap (the persist-debounce case needs a real-time Main — an `UnconfinedTestDispatcher` clock never advances by sleeping). | 2026-07-03 | **PA.6 hotfix — the Qwen light tier shipped dead on 100% of its target segment; root cause, remedy, and the two bent rules.** User device report: Gemma worked, but a downloaded Qwen still showed "No AI provider is set up yet". **Root cause:** `AppModule`'s `onDeviceReady = { gemma.isReady() \|\| nano.isReady() }` — written correctly in P2.2 when exactly two engines existed — was never updated when PA.3a appended `QwenEngine` to the `OnDeviceProvider` engines list *in the same file, 164 lines above*. The bug class: **"an engine list grew, a hand-enumerated seam didn't."** Impact stated plainly: on the 3–4 GB segment the tier exists for, Gemma is structurally ineligible (4096 floor), Nano is flagship-only, and `usable()` routed even an explicit on-device selection through the broken seam — **no user workaround; the tier only ever worked when masked by a coexisting ready engine.** **How it slipped:** every test layer faked the seam as a boolean; the only real-DI-graph test is `@Ignore`d; and the K10 device run had **Gemma coexisting**, so resolution passed via Gemma while `preferredTier` steered to Qwen inside the provider — the tier-alone configuration was never exercised. Two loop rules bent: SPEC §3 never gained the LIGHT tier (spec-same-commit), and adjacent ledger items J9/J12 weren't refreshed (rule-11's letter was followed for K10 only). **Remedy (structural over one-liner):** `OnDeviceProvider.isReady()` = the single readiness source; the resolver seam delegates; a composition test executes the real `@Provides` bodies Qwen-only; a structural test makes hand-enumeration a red build; SPEC/VERIFICATION/CLAUDE.md retro-synced; a process memory now requires **consumer-sweeps when an abstraction's summary changes** and **tier-alone device verification for additive tiers**. **Live bonus find (emulator, this session):** at 88% disk, the first `Engine.initialize()` **SIGABRT-crashed the app** writing its XNNPack cache → `EngineCachePreflight` refuses gracefully (`AppError.Storage`). Deferred (tracked, PR-2 + backlog): per-model notification IDs, tier-scoped Test button, download-completion feedback, tier-naming/ineligible-copy polish, cancel-download (the shipped Background-activity cancel is a placebo for model downloads — first-priority backlog), Ask-sheet download-awareness + tier indicator, onboarding line, resolver-seam factory hardening, ghost empty-assistant-bubble cleanup after a mid-stream crash. |
| 2026-06-27 | **P-HTML PH.5 shipped — offline figures via `data:`-inline (the fork resolved *against* the SPEC's reserved virtual origin).** Planned via an Ultracode pass (map incl. live arXiv/ar5iv research → 3 design stances → a 3-lens adversarial judge → synthesis) **then a personal adversarial validation.** **Decisive finding:** an https **virtual origin** (the SPEC's reserved PH.5 mechanism) is suppressed by `blockNetworkImage=true` (verified AOSP semantics), so it would force `blockNetworkImage=false` — *disarming a standing egress control* — whereas **`data:`-inline** keeps **both** `blockNetworkLoads` and `blockNetworkImage` armed with `baseUrl=null` (opaque origin, no SOP/fetch surface), needs **no new dep**, no `shouldInterceptRequest`, no `file://`. So PH.5 base64-inlines pre-fetched figure bytes into `index.html` (pure transform tokenizes `<img>` + manifest → `HtmlImageFetcher` → pure `HtmlImageInliner`), two-phase (text-first, then figures). **My validation caught 3 load-bearing bugs in the workflow blueprint:** (1) the resolution base must be the **exact fetched page URL** (native `…/html/<id>v<ver>`, no trailing slash, version-prefixed srcs) — the blueprint's `…/<id>v<ver>/` base **doubles** the version dir (confirmed by live-fetching arxiv.org/ar5iv); (2) the two-phase re-store overwrites `index.html`, which `File.renameTo` won't do on the **Windows JVM test host** → `Files.move(REPLACE_EXISTING)`; (3) `withTimeoutOrNull(fetchAll())` **discards partials** → the fetcher emits per-image via a callback so the deadline keeps what's fetched. **Caps PROVISIONAL** (count 40 / 600 KB / 4 MB / 30 s; ctor-injectable) → device-ratify (HUMAN.md). **No red-line escalation** (data: needs no sign-off; the virtual-origin path *would* have). Harvested 6 in-vision deferrals to the backlog (figure-refresh, priority limiter, image crawl-delay, inline-SVG→PH.8, blank-slot CLS, streaming inline). Full `./gradlew build` green; SPEC §8/§9/§10/§12 updated; device checks → `VERIFICATION.md §M` M-PH5-1…6. |

| 2026-06-26 | **PS.4b shipped — image export pivoted from a JS render-signal to host-driven capture (device truth, K17).** The planned capture (and PS.4a's `arxiver://rendered` JS signal) assumed the off-screen WebView would tick `requestAnimationFrame` so the page could self-signal "rendered". **Device verification proved that false:** an invisible/occluded WebView produces no frames, so rAF callbacks never run — and at `alpha=0` Chromium throttles the page's `setTimeout` timers too — so *neither* the ready-poll *nor* the 4 s safety path (both rAF-wrapped) ever fired (the on-screen `arxiver://height` direct-`location.href` pings *did* fire, proving JS ran but frames/timers were starved). **Resolution:** the **host** owns capture — render at `alpha=0.004` (non-zero so the compositor keeps producing frames → Mermaid/fonts actually finish), poll **host-initiated `evaluateJavascript`** for "fonts loaded + every Mermaid `<svg>` present" (host-initiated eval is immune to the renderer's hidden-page throttling), then snapshot. Two further device bugs fixed: the captured height clipped the last node (a Mermaid `<svg>` **overflows its body box** → measure the **max element bottom**, not `body.getBoundingClientRect().height`), and the share-chooser **preview** hit a FileProvider `SecurityException` (grant reaches the target but not the preview process → also set **`ClipData`**). The dead `forCapture` script + `RichRenderSignal.heightPx` were removed (honest cleanup; `deviceHeightPx` + the FileProvider stay). Net: a faithful full-answer PNG (light + dark) with a working chooser preview — `VERIFICATION.md` K17 + log. The original "off-screen→PNG on a causal JS signal" plan was *directionally* right (off-screen→PNG, wait-for-render) but the *signal carrier* had to move from page-JS to host-poll once hardware showed page timers/rAF don't run off-screen. |
| 2026-06-26 | **Phase P-Share planned + scoped (Ultracode, user-directed).** The three deferred P-Rich follow-ons (R2.5 svg · R4.2 export · R4-TTS) reshaped + expanded into a cohesive **"export / share / act on everything"** phase. A 14-agent Ultracode planning workflow (4 surface maps → 6 designs incl. a 3-stance R4.2 capture fork → 3 judge lenses → synthesis) produced the plan. **Decisive judge finding (web-verified):** `createPrintDocumentAdapter` triggers from `onPageFinished` = HTML *loaded*, not async-JS *rendered* — so the ROADMAP's old "prefer print-adapter→PDF" steer for R4.2 was **wrong** (it doesn't beat the `arxiver://height` race, just hides it). | 2026-06-26 | **P-Atlas PA.5b shipped — clustering + LoD, with a label-propagation→Louvain pivot.** The blueprint specified label propagation for community detection. Implemented + tested, it revealed a fatal flaw under the determinism constraint: a **deterministic min-label tie-break makes LP flood across any bridge**, so any connected graph collapses to a single community (≈ connected-components). That makes the overview a useless single blob for a richly-connected collection *and* makes the "bundled inter-cluster meta-edge" feature dead (distinct clusters would only ever be disconnected components with no crossing edges). **Pivoted to deterministic Louvain modularity local-moving** (each node greedily moves to the neighbour community with the largest `k_i,in − Σtot·k_i/2m` gain; prefer-stay on tie, smallest-id on remaining ties → order-independent): modularity correctly subdivides a connected mass, so a single citation bridge between two dense topics stays two clusters and meta-edges are meaningful. Verified by a failing-then-passing meta-edge test (two triangles + one bridge → 2 clusters + 1 weighted meta-edge). Pipeline = `GraphSceneBuilder.build` (prune → `GraphLayoutEngine.layout` → `GraphClusterer.cluster`); pruning bounds similarity to top-`SIMILAR_K=4`/node above `0.3` (citations kept whole). LoD baked on `GraphScene`: overview ≤`OVERVIEW_MAX=12` (top-11 cluster super-nodes + one "Unconnected (N)" bucket, crossing edges bundled per group-pair) → mid (top-degree labelled) → detail (all). `primary_category` fallback only when edgeless. 17 new pure-JVM tests; full `./gradlew build` green; no device surface. Category data threaded via a new optional `RelationNode.primaryCategory` (default null → PA.1 unaffected). |
| 2026-06-26 | **P-Atlas PA.5 direction set + PA.5a shipped — collection knowledge-map via "layout-as-data" (Ultracode-designed, user-approved).** An 11-agent Ultracode workflow (4 Explore surface-maps → 3 diverse designs → 3 adversarial judge-lenses → synthesis) resolved the rendering-tech fork. Scores: **Design C (precomputed layout-as-data + thin Compose Canvas) 25** > A (live Compose force-sim) 21 > B (bundled graph-lib in WebView) 19; C placed first-or-tied on every lens. **Why C:** making layout a *pure deterministic function* turns "is this node-soup at N=300?" into a JVM golden you eyeball off-device, and lands the whole risky-correctness surface in two pure, device-free, golden-tested PRs before any renderer exists — matching A's red-line cleanliness (zero deps/assets, no socket on the draw path, airplane-mode-identical) while shrinking A's untestable on-device interaction code to "does a dumb blitter pan." B loses on a perpetual minified-dependency offline/no-telemetry audit tax. **Grafts:** from A — an "Unconnected (N)" super-node for isolated papers, a "+N more" drill-in budget, and a mandatory CI-testable "View as list" a11y fallback; from B — only the *discipline* (pinned-SHA + build-failing source-scan) as the bar *if* a JS dep is ever proposed. **User-approved forks (all recommended option):** full-screen nav destination (canvas can't share the Ask sheet's vertical scroll); augment—not replace—the Connections list; hard-cap ~400 nodes by centrality. **Self-decided:** scene re-derived from cache on config-change (not parcelled) to dodge the Binder limit. PA.1's Mermaid star is kept as the single-paper/airplane static fallback (not replaced). **PA.5a impl deviations from the blueprint (deliberate, recorded):** (1) **naïve O(n²) FR repulsion, no Barnes–Hut quadtree** — the ~400 cap bounds cost and the naïve form is *more* obviously deterministic; the quadtree is a deferred perf lever, not correctness; (2) the "50-node JSON snapshot" is asserted as **structural legibility invariants** (min pairwise ≥10, real 2D extent, determinism, order-invariance) rather than a brittle exact-bytes FP golden — keeps CI robust across the Linux-runner/Windows-dev split I can't pre-verify, while `StrictMath` + 2dp rounding still buys bit-determinism. `GraphScene` made `@Serializable` (kotlinx added to `:core:search`) for the PA.5b/c cache + eyeballable JSON. `GraphLayoutEngineTest` 12/0/0, full `./gradlew build` green. |
| 2026-06-26 | **P-Atlas PA.4 shipped — "app-draws-the-structure" tables (Ultracode-designed).** Extended PA.1's deterministic-artifact thesis to tables. Designed via an Ultracode workflow (4 Explore agents mapped the splice/prompt/render/richness surfaces → 3 diverse designs (minimal / robust / north-star) → a synthesized blueprint that resolved the cross-design forks against the code). **Decisions:** (1) home = **`:core:ai`** (owns `OutputRichness`, no `:app` edge) not `:core:search`; (2) sentinel = the composite **`~|~`** (collision-proof vs math `|x|`/code/markdown, survives any tokenizer) not `~~` (GFM strikethrough) or a fragile Unicode glyph; (3) a **block fence** `TABLE::`/`::TABLE` (line-anchored like the proven `FOLLOWUPS::`) not a per-line marker; (4) **no reformat re-ask** in PA.4 (keeps the transform pure; it's a PA.5 lever owned by the repository). The model emits the low-syntax intermediate (research arXiv:2506.19512: small models nail simple delimited formats 0-shot); a pure `StructuredTableTransform.transform(String):String` parses → `ComparisonTable(header, rows, parseConfidence)` → guaranteed-valid GFM, or a grounded bulleted list below `CONFIDENCE_FLOOR=0.70`. **Splice:** a shared `settleStructured(prepared, body)` gated on the new `PreparedChat.richness == STRUCTURED`, called at BOTH the persist seam (`ChatRepository.stream` Done) and the display seam (`AskViewModel.settleFollowUps`) on the same `extractFollowUps(...).first` input → DB == UI == export; FULL/PLAIN/no-fence bodies are byte-identical (redaction goldens untouched, verified by a FULL-byte-identical repo golden). Rendering reuses the existing `MarkdownText` GFM path (zero render-code change). The STRUCTURED addendum grew (~50→~130 tok teaching the format) → the PA.0a budget test was made **self-adjusting** (asserts the drop ≤ addendum_tokens/chunk_tokens). Tests: `StructuredTableTransformTest` 20/0/0 + `ChatRepositoryTest` 9/0/0 (STRUCTURED-persists-a-table, FULL-byte-identical, the shared-`settleStructured`-gate) + `ChatContextAssembler` 22/0/0. **Pre-merge adversarial review** (3 dims, each finding verified): 0 blockers; **1 major caught** — a reviewer *empirically compiled+ran commonmark* and proved a GFM table glued directly under prose (no blank line) folds into a paragraph and renders as literal pipes → fixed by inserting blank-line separation around the rendered block (the golden had hidden it with a hard-coded `\n\n`); + 8 minor/nit folded in (`cleanCell` balanced-strip so `0.94*` survives, unclosed-fence + 0.70-boundary + mid-line-mention + display-seam goldens, doc guards). Device adherence → `VERIFICATION.md` K11. |

| 2026-06-26 | **P-Atlas PA.0 spike resolved + PA.4 pivoted to "app-draws-the-structure" (away from constrained decoding).** A multi-workflow deep-research pass (web/arXiv/HF, free-text agents after schema-degeneration, primary-source verified) closed both open gates. **PA.0b — light tier NOT blocked:** `litert-community/Qwen3-0.6B` ships a CPU-capable `Qwen3-0.6B.litertlm` (614 MB INT8, community-benchmarked ~212/13 tok/s on CPU; verified the file list directly via the HF tree API). This makes invalid tables structurally impossible, is north-star-aligned, pure-`:core`/offline/zero-new-runtime, and off-device golden-testable. Constrained decoding is rejected not just as unavailable but as the **wrong tool** at our scale — it trades content for syntax ("Constraint Tax" 2026 on Qwen-0.5B/1.5B: validity→100% but accuracy 19.7%→11.0%, wrong-but-valid 49.5%→88.9%; "Let Me Speak Freely?" arXiv:2408.02442 / CRANE / DCCD all say decouple reasoning from formatting). **Rejected alternatives:** a 2nd runtime (llama.cpp/MLC/ONNX-GenAI all fail ≥1 of {native-Kotlin, CPU, sub-2B, no-JNI}), a custom JNI LLGuidance shim (buys syntax the app already guarantees free). **Watch-items only:** #1662, and fine-tuning (FunctionGemma-270M 58%→85%) as the model-side lever if a tier ever *must* emit structure. PA.3 stays `richness=PLAIN` and is re-scoped to the 2–4 GB device segment (an additive light tier on a lower RAM floor, not a smaller Gemma). Docs/decision PR (no code); the empirical Qwen-load + intermediate-adherence legs ride PA.3/PA.4 device testing (`VERIFICATION.md`). |
| 2026-06-26 | **P-Atlas PA.2 shipped — per-engine output-richness ladder (`OutputRichness {PLAIN, STRUCTURED, FULL}`).** Replaced the binary cloud-vs-on-device rich-output gate with a per-engine ladder: `OutputRichness` is an **abstract** `val` on `OnDeviceEngine` (Gemma=STRUCTURED, Nano=PLAIN) and a **non-defaulted** field on `ProviderCapability` — the non-default is the point: the compiler then forces every one of the 4 cloud-capability builders (incl. `ChatRepositoryTest`'s, which the first pass missed) to declare `FULL`, killing the silent-PLAIN-default footgun the stress-test flagged. **Resolution = Option B** (refining the ROADMAP's earlier "eager-resolve-reused-by-`chat()`" sketch): `OnDeviceProvider.resolveRichness()` runs the **same** extracted `pickReadyEngine()` as `chat()`, and `ChatRepository.prepare` overrides the on-device capability via `copy(richness=…)` before assembling. The microscopic prepare-vs-stream readiness flip is **confirmed benign** — STRUCTURED differs from PLAIN only by a table nudge and the base prompt already invites tables for every engine — so Option A (binding the engine into `PreparedChat`) is needless complexity. The single `ChatContextAssembler` gate widened to 3 states; **cloud FULL is byte-identical** (`ChatPreviewBuilder`/`PayloadBuilder` redaction goldens green). **Research-reshaped scope** (2025–2026 web/arXiv): the 1-shot table **exemplar moved *into* PA.2** STRUCTURED (the one lever that lifts ~2B table validity) while Mermaid (~60% valid) + LaTeX (~9.7% error) stay cloud-only; consequently **PA.4 was reframed** from "few-shot exemplars" to the real valid-by-construction win (**grammar/constrained decoding** via LiteRT-LM's LLGuidance), gated on PA.0c confirming the Kotlin binding exposes it. **PA.0a (done):** the RAG-budget half is a **headless CI test** (the ~50-token nudge drops no chunk at the 4096 on-device window); the table-validity half is **`[E]`-verified** (`VERIFICATION.md` K9, 2026-06-26) — on `emulator-5554` (once another local session's `dev.helpinghand.companion` agent vacated it for its own emulator), Gemma E2B emitted a **valid 2×2 Markdown table** for a comparison question in Standard mode, stayed **grounded** (cited `[1]`, refused to fabricate a comparison absent from the abstract), and used **no LaTeX/Mermaid** — confirming the ~2B-with-exemplar table prediction on our real build. | 2026-06-25 | **P-Rich R3d.3 — privacy-preview disclosure + assembler/repo plumbing.** Third vision phase: the seam that lets an image reach a turn, plus the "what leaves the device" honesty contract. `assemble(..., attachment: ChatImage? = null)` and `prepare(..., attachment: ChatImage? = null)` are optional/defaulted so every existing caller compiles and a no-attachment call is **byte-identical** (redaction goldens untouched). **Defense-in-depth, two layers:** `ChatRepository.prepare` already drops the image if the resolved provider lacks vision (comment-documented), and the assembler **independently** re-checks — `images = if (attachment != null && capability.vision) listOf(attachment) else emptyList()` — so even a caller that passes an image to an on-device/non-vision provider never reaches the wire. The `ChatPreviewBuilder` discloses the attachment in **both** surfaces the user/golden see — the human `text` (`[Attached image: page N of arXiv:… — image/jpeg, ~KB]`) and the golden `json` (a new optional `attachments: List<String>?`, omitted for text-only turns via `explicitNulls=false` so the existing goldens stay byte-identical) — computed from label/mime/`base64.length`, **never** the base64 bytes themselves. Unit-verified: assembler folds the image onto the final user turn for a vision cap, drops it for a non-vision cap, and a null attachment matches the no-arg call; a sentinel-base64 `ChatPreviewBuilderTest` asserts the label/mime appear in both `text` and `json` while the bytes appear in **neither** (the R3d red line). No device surface (dead code until R3d.4 wires the UI). The known `UncaughtExceptionsBeforeTest` flake recurred once (`ChatRepositoryTest`/`testReleaseUnitTest`) and cleared on a clean re-run; a mid-session machine restart left the branch + 5 working-tree edits intact. Remaining: R3d.4 (preset + page-pick UI + on-device vision E2E — the flagship). |
| 2026-06-24 | **P-Rich R3d.2 — PDF page → vision image (`PageImageSource`).** Second vision phase, isolating all Android/bitmap/lifecycle risk. An injected `PageImageSource` (interface + `PdfPageImageSource` impl + Hilt provide) renders a paper's PDF page to a downscaled JPEG `ChatImage`. Key stress-test fixes baked in: **M1** — the local-PDF check is **network-free** (globs `filesDir/pdfs/<id>v*.pdf` rather than calling the network-refreshing `PaperRepository.paper()`), so gating/rendering never trips the arXiv rate limiter; **M5** — `eraseColor(WHITE)` before render (JPEG has no alpha, else transparent page regions encode black behind figures); **m4** — cap the **long** edge (≤1568px, both providers' downscale point) not just width, via a pure `cappedSize` helper. A fresh `PdfRenderer`+fd per call on IO, closed in `finally` (no sharing with the viewer's private holder). Dead code until R3d.4; pure `cappedSize` unit-tested; live render verified at R3d.4. |
| 2026-06-24 | **P-Rich R3d.1 — multimodal request model + vision capability (core:ai foundation, Ultracode-designed).** First of 4 trust-boundary phases for vision (workflow: 3 surface maps → synthesis → adversarial stress-test that flagged 8 must-fixes). R3d.1 carries the riskiest change — the byte-identity contract of two shipping providers — but has **zero runtime effect** (nothing builds a non-empty `images` list until R3d.4). Added `ChatImage(mediaType, base64, label?)`, `ChatMessage.images = emptyList()`, `ProviderCapability.vision = false`. Decisive serialization detail: Anthropic's `WireMessage.content` became a `JsonElement` so a text-only turn encodes as a JSON **string** (byte-identical) and an image turn as a content-block **array**; Gemini keeps its **unconditional** text `GenPart` (stress-test C2 — an `isNotEmpty()` guard would have changed the empty-content wire) and appends `inlineData` parts (null fields omitted by `encodeDefaults=false`). `vision=true` for Claude/Gemini, default false on-device. The human `label` is dropped on the wire (set only for the R3d.3 privacy preview). Tests assert text-only byte-identity (string not array; no `inlineData`), mixed-content serialization, and label-never-on-wire for both providers. The known `UncaughtExceptionsBeforeTest` flake recurred (2 suites) and cleared on re-run. Remaining: R3d.2 (PDF→image), R3d.3 (privacy disclosure + plumbing), R3d.4 (preset + UI + on-device E2E). |
| 2026-06-24 | **P-Rich R4 — save/export/share (text/Markdown) shipped & emulator-verified (Ultracode-designed).** Delivers the user's original "save/export/share" ask. A 5-agent workflow (3 surface maps → synthesis → adversarial stress-test) set a robust MVP: **text/Markdown only via the OS share sheet** — answer→Markdown + conversation→Markdown — deferring image/PDF (R4.2) because the only robust WebView capture is a print-flow PDF and the off-screen bitmap path races async Mermaid. A pure, testable `ConversationMarkdown` serializer reuses the existing `ACTION_SEND`+`EXTRA_TEXT` pattern (new `Context.shareText`), so **no FileProvider/manifest/dependency change**. Stress-test catches fixed before coding: ChatHistoryScreen had no callback to "mirror" (added `LocalContext`+wiring); share reads `message.text` not the rendered `body`, and the serializer defensively re-strips a `FOLLOWUPS::` sentinel (covers the cancelled-cloud-Max partial that `finally` doesn't strip); a single shared `truncateExcerpt` backs both on-screen `CitationSources` and the export so they can't drift. **Red-line judgment recorded:** the "chat excluded from exports" rule targets the *automated, importable backup schema* (`BackupManager`/`LibraryExporter`); a user-initiated one-shot `ACTION_SEND` of a single conversation is categorically different and is the user's explicit ask — a standalone serializer keeps the backup wall intact (clarified in a `ChatEntities.kt` comment). Verified on-device: chooser opens above the modal sheet with a full correct transcript, no sentinel leak. Known limitations logged: resumed-history exports carry inline `[n]` without a Sources block (citations live-only), and `text/plain` shows raw markdown in non-markdown recipients. Two build-gate nits fixed (a >120 line; an unused `cd_` string → UnusedResources lint) + my own wrong test assertion (`"## You".startsWith("#")`). |
| 2026-06-24 | **P-Rich R3b.2 — follow-up chips shipped & emulator-verified (Ultracode-designed).** The other half of the mode idea. Designed via a Workflow (2 parallel mechanism designers → synthesis → adversarial stress-test); the stress-test caught two ship-blockers before implementation: **(C1)** the cloud path streams from `confirmSend()`, not `ask()`, so the mode must be **pinned** (`pendingMode`) onto the parked request and threaded into `startStream` — otherwise every cloud-Max turn silently degrades to heuristic chips; **(C2)** the `FOLLOWUPS::` extractor must be **final-line-only with heuristic fallback**, else a mid-answer/fenced sentinel truncates the conclusion or diverges between display and DB. Final design: a pure `FollowUpHeuristics` (Quick/Standard/on-device — template selection de-duped vs the asked + prior-session questions, a true floor backstop so it never drops below 2, and a non-ASCII guard so a non-English answer shows no mismatched English chips) and a shared pure `extractFollowUps` used by **both** the ViewModel (display) and `ChatRepository` (persist) so the rendered and stored bodies always agree. `MAX_FOLLOWUPS_SUFFIX` is appended only in the cloud-Max branch (rides the user turn → goldens untouched; on-device omitted so small models aren't pushed to emit broken sentinels — model path gated `MAX && isCloud`). Chips re-enter `ask()` via `runPreset` and render only on the latest assistant turn. Verified on-device: Standard heuristic chips + tap-to-ask; cloud-Max model chips with the sentinel stripped (no leak), composing with R2 (the Max answer drew a Mermaid diagram). A test name with a `;` broke the JVM compile (illegal identifier char) — renamed. P-Rich conversational surface is now complete. |
| 2026-06-24 | **P-Rich R3b — 3-mode depth dial shipped & emulator-verified.** The "how" dimension (the user's mode idea). `ChatMode { QUICK, STANDARD, MAX }` lives in the `chat` package — the assembler is the right home because it already owns provider-aware prompt logic (the `CLOUD_RICH_ADDENDUM` gate). The mode resolves to a directive **prepended to the user turn** (not the system prompt): Standard → `""` → byte-identical request, so the redaction goldens and today's behavior are untouched; Quick → terse; Max → detailed + a **cloud-only** table/Mermaid nudge (so on-device Gemma, which has no rich invite, isn't pushed toward broken markup — the directive is computed provider-awarely from `capability.onDevice`). Threaded `mode` through `prepare()` → `assemble()`, all with defaults so every existing caller/test compiled unchanged. UI: a `SingleChoiceSegmentedButtonRow` between the R3c preset row and the notes toggle; mode applies to both typed questions and presets (the preset × mode grid). Verified on-device via the privacy preview (Max prepends its directive incl. the nudge; SYSTEM unchanged). Two ktlint line-length/arg-wrap nits in the new code were auto-fixed with `ktlintFormat`. **Follow-up chips deferred to R3b.2** (answer-bubble extraction is its own concern; Max is already meaningful without them). |
| 2026-06-24 | **P-Rich R3c — Ask preset library shipped & emulator-verified.** Implemented the "what" dimension as the simplest correct thing: a preset is a **predefined question**. The existing `summarize()` was literally `ask(SUMMARIZE_PROMPT)`, so the library is an `AskPresets` registry of (UI label, model-facing instruction) and tapping a chip calls `runPreset(instruction)` → the same grounded `ask()`. Consequence: **no `ChatContextAssembler` change and the redaction goldens are untouched** — a preset request is byte-identical to typing the same text (confirmed on-device: the privacy preview showed the preset instruction as the `Question:` with the `SYSTEM:` prompt unchanged). Labels live in `strings.xml`; instructions are English Kotlin constants matching the `SUMMARIZE_PROMPT` precedent (model-facing, not localized). The chip row is scope-filtered via `AskPresets.forScope(scope is RetrievalScope.Paper)` (paper-only presets — Explain method, Limitations, BibTeX, Reproducibility — drop out of collection chat) and disabled while streaming; computed at the `AskSheet` call site and passed down (the private `AskSheetContent` can't see the scope). `summarize()` kept as a thin alias so its existing test stays green. The known intermittent `ChatRepositoryTest` flake recurred once in `testReleaseUnitTest` and cleared on re-run (unrelated to R3c). Next: R3b (the orthogonal "how" / mode dial). |

| 2026-06-23 | **P-Rich R1 — math rendering (KaTeX) shipped + emulator-verified.** Decision on the inline-math fork: a native bitmap lib (jlatexmath) is dep-risky (not reliably on Maven Central) and awkward for inline `$…$`; instead a **math-containing answer is rendered whole** through a sandboxed offline `RichBlockWebView` (commonmark `HtmlRenderer` → HTML → bundled KaTeX), while plain answers stay on the native R0 renderer. | 2026-06-19 | **Phase F2 — on-device chat fixed from a device bug report.** Per-paper + collection chat returned blank answers on the S20. Logcat root cause: the pinned `gemma-4-E2B-it-web.litertlm` is the **WebGPU** build (`gpu_artisan` decoder only); on the CPU backend (`npu_registry: NPU could not be loaded` → `backend: CPU`) the loader logs `TF_LITE_PREFILL_DECODE not found … Skipping` → zero tokens. Decisions: (1) **swap `GemmaEngine.SPEC` to the standard CPU/GPU `gemma-4-E2B-it.litertlm`** (2.59 GB, SHA `18193810…63c`), pinned + guarded by `GemmaSpecTest` (no `-web` regression); the `-web`/chip-specific NPU builds are wrong for a generic CPU device. (2) **Zero tokens = failure, not a blank answer:** `GemmaEngine`/`NanoEngine` throw `AiException` when a stream yields nothing (latent since P1.2b — they always emitted a clean `Done`), and `AskViewModel` guards an empty `Done` too (cloud defense-in-depth) → the error toast shows instead of a blank bubble, and "Test connection" stops falsely reporting success. (3) **`ModelDownloader` purges stale same-extension siblings on (re)download** (extension-scoped, so the bge `.onnx` is safe) so the model swap doesn't strand the old ~2 GB file. Model swap is the real fix; (2)/(3) are robustness. Device confirmation gated in `VERIFICATION.md §J6/§K3`. |

| 2026-06-15 | **P2.2 built** (chat orchestration + history + privacy preview) — **second real Room migration** (v2→v3). Decisions: (1) **Provider resolution** (user-chosen): respect the explicit `selectedAiProvider` by default; a new **`preferOnDeviceWhenReady`** preference (default off, plumbed in `AiProviderStore`/`SettingsRepository`) makes an on-device engine win when ready — the Settings **toggle UI** rides with P2.3. On-device readiness is the engines' `isReady()`, not `ProviderRegistry.isConfigured` (a key-less provider always reports configured), so `ProviderResolver` takes an explicit `onDeviceReady` seam. (2) **Partial turns persist** with a `chat_messages.status` (`complete`/`incomplete`/`error`) so a cancelled/failed stream survives in history; cleanup writes use `NonCancellable`. (3) **`ChatRepository` split `prepare` (read-only: embed→retrieve→assemble→resolve→preview) vs `stream` (persists + streams)** so declining the "what leaves the device" confirm persists nothing and the query isn't re-embedded. | 2026-06-15 | **P2.1 built** (on-device RAG retrieval foundation) — **first real Room migration** (v1→v2). Decisions: (1) `chunk_embeddings` mirrors `paper_embeddings` (BLOB float32, per-row `model`/`dim` guard, `deleteByModelMismatch` — no separate `embedding_meta` table) but adds an autogenerated `id` rowid so an external-content **FTS4 `chunk_fts`** can index `chunk_text`; `(paper_id, source_kind, ordinal)` is unique so re-index is delete-then-insert. (2) **Hybrid retrieval** (user-chosen): semantic cosine + `chunk_fts` BM25 fused by the existing `HybridFusion` (keyed on chunk id) — reused unchanged. (3) **Eager library backfill** (user-chosen): chunk indexing folded into `EmbeddingWorker` (reuses the one loaded ONNX session + unmetered job, bounded `CHUNK_BACKFILL_PER_RUN`); ad-hoc papers index on demand via `RagIndexer`. (4) Layering: `TextChunker`/`RagRetriever` in `:core:search` (depends on `:core:database`+`:core:ml`), pure-testable behind `ChunkVectorSource`/`ChunkKeywordSource` seams; `RagIndexer` orchestration in `:app` (mirrors `EmbeddingWorker`), embeds via an injected `embed` seam (`EmbeddingService::embedPassages`) so it's faked in CI (no ONNX). (5) `Migration1To2` SQL is kept byte-identical to Room's generated `2.json` (incl. FTS triggers); validated in CI by `Migration1To2Test` (`MigrationTestHelper` under Robolectric, schemas exposed via the `test` asset srcDir) — the convention's androidTest deferral was unnecessary once the schema assets were wired. (6) `chunker`/`retriever` char-budget chunking is a tokenizer-free proxy for bge's 512-token window (keeps `:core:search` ONNX-free). New backlog: a **background-tasks monitor UI** (user-floated). |
| 2026-06-15 | **P2 planned at phase level** (`docs/P2-PLAN.md`); ROADMAP P2 expanded into four PR-sized subphases (P2.1 retrieval foundation → P2.2 chat orchestration/history/privacy-preview → P2.3 per-paper Ask → P2.4 collections-as-KBs) + CHECKPOINT P2. Decisions (user-confirmed): (1) **knowledge base = an existing Collection** (per-collection chat scope; per-paper Ask needs no KB) — reuses `collection_papers` membership, so no new curation UI/schema; a **library-wide KB flag** (`library_entries.in_kb`) is deferred to the v2 infra backlog. (2) **Build order: per-paper Ask ships first** (narrowest high-value surface), collections-as-KBs next. (3) **This is a lean docs-only PR** — the overarching plan + ROADMAP/VERIFICATION alignment now; detailed contract specs (SPEC-SEARCH §8 chunking, SPEC-DATA `chunk_embeddings`/`chat_sessions`/`chat_messages` DDL + migrations) ride with each subphase's implementation PR. (4) Retrieval stays **on-device only** (only retrieved chunks + the question may reach a cloud provider, behind a "what leaves the device" confirm — the preview P1.1 deferred to P2); P2 adds **no new allowed hosts** (provider endpoints landed in P1). New device-bound checks seeded in `VERIFICATION.md` §K. |
| 2026-06-15 | **P1.2c built** (system Gemini Nano, Tier 1) — **P1 complete**. Decisions: (1) **default on-device order reversed to Gemma → Nano** (user-chosen): Nano's ML Kit Prompt API caps output ~256 tokens and validates EN/KO only, too tight for paper summaries; Gemma (when downloaded) is the better on-device engine, Nano the zero-download fallback. Updated `TierSelector`, SPEC-AI-PROVIDERS §3, and the ordering tests together. (2) **User-selectable preferred on-device engine** (Auto/Gemma/Nano) persisted as `preferred_ondevice_tier`; `OnDeviceProvider` resolves preference-then-default among *ready* engines via a `suspend () -> InferenceTier?` supplier (no `runBlocking`). (3) ML Kit `genai-prompt:1.0.0-beta2`; inspected the real AAR (`Generation.getClient()` → suspend `checkStatus(): @FeatureStatus Int`, `download(): Flow<DownloadStatus>`, `generateContentStream(String): Flow<GenerateContentResponse>` with `candidates[].text`) — the `-Xskip-metadata-version-check` flag from P1.2b also covers it. Adding the dep is safe on non-flagships (checkStatus → UNAVAILABLE → degrade to Gemma/cloud). |
| 2026-06-15 | **P1.2b built** (Gemma 4 E2B on-device, Tier 2). Decisions: (1) on-device engines + provider + probe live in `:core:ai` (consistent with the cloud providers); `:core:ai` gains `implementation(project(":core:ml"))` (ModelDownloader/ModelState reuse) + `litertlm-android:0.13.1`. (2) **Kotlin metadata gotcha:** LiteRT-LM 0.13.1 ships Kotlin **2.3.0** metadata; our toolchain is 2.1.21 (reads ≤2.2.0), so `:core:ai` adds `-Xskip-metadata-version-check` — scoped to the one consuming module rather than a project-wide Kotlin bump (we only consume its public API). (3) Model = user-chosen **text-only** `gemma-4-E2B-it-web.litertlm` (~1.87 GB, SHA `3a08e8d9…`); it's WebGPU-tuned so Android CPU loadability is **device-unverified** — fallback to the standard `gemma-4-E2B-it.litertlm` (2.59 GB) recorded in VERIFICATION.md. CPU backend (GPU/NPU later). (4) Two `ModelDownloader` singletons distinguished by a `@GemmaModel` qualifier. (5) Narrow seams `OnDeviceEngine`/`OnDeviceModelController`/`DeviceCapabilityProbe` keep the engine device-bound while the provider, settings VM, and tiering are pure-JVM CI tests. |
| 2026-06-15 | **P1.2 planned + P1.2a built** (on-device inference tiering core). Research confirmed (post-cutoff): **Gemma 4** released 2026-03-31 under **Apache-2.0** (E2B/E4B `.litertlm` for LiteRT-LM; `litert-community/gemma-4-E2B-it-litert-lm`) — the spec's "Gemma 4 E2B" is correct; and the system-Nano path is the **ML Kit GenAI Prompt API** (`com.google.mlkit:genai-prompt:1.0.0-beta2`). External-API reference committed at `docs/reference/on-device-ai.md`. Decisions: (1) on-device tiering split into P1.2a (pure CI-testable core) → P1.2b (Gemma/LiteRT-LM, Tier 2) → P1.2c (Nano/ML Kit, Tier 1); user chose **both** on-device tiers. (2) `DeviceCapability` carries `gemmaReady: Boolean` (not `:core:ml` `ModelState`) so `:core:ai` stays free of the ONNX dep; the app probe maps `ModelState`→ready. (3) `TierSelector.recommend = fallbackOrder.first()`, tiers listed only when usable, always ending NONE. (4) RAM floor `GEMMA_RAM_FLOOR_MB = 4096` (Gemma's Android runtime ≈1.4–1.7 GB). (5) On-device engines live in `:core:ai` (native libs only reach `:app`); the Android `DeviceCapabilityProbe` impl lives in `:app` (needs `ActivityManager`/ML Kit/downloader). |
| 2026-06-15 | **P1.1b built** (Gemini transport + provider registry + Settings "AI providers" UX). Decisions: (1) two narrow interfaces keep the ViewModel a pure-JVM test — `AiKeyStore` (impl `AiKeyVault`) for keys and `AiProviderStore` (impl `SettingsRepository`) for the default selection — added after the real `EncryptedSharedPreferences` threw `NoSuchAlgorithmException` under the **:app** Robolectric env (it works under :core:ai's, so `AiKeyVaultTest`/`ProviderRegistryTest` still exercise the real crypto there). (2) Default selection persisted in DataStore (`selected_ai_provider`); first provider connected auto-becomes default. (3) Test-connection fires a tiny real ping (16 tokens) through the provider; HTTP {400,401,403} → "key rejected" (Gemini returns 400 API_KEY_INVALID, Anthropic 401/403), offline → "offline", else → generic error. (4) Pinned `gemini-2.0-flash`; model picker is a later enhancement. (5) `ProviderRegistry` lists providers + `isConfigured`; the selected default lives in app settings, not the registry, to keep `:core:ai` free of `:app` deps. |
| 2026-06-15 | **P1.1a built** (`:core:ai` + Claude transport). Decisions: (1) `AnthropicProvider` takes a key **supplier** `() -> String?` rather than the vault directly — keeps the transport decoupled from key storage and its MockWebServer tests free of `EncryptedSharedPreferences`; DI wires `{ aiKeyVault.get(CLAUDE) }`. (2) Manual SSE line-parse over the OkHttp body (no `okhttp-sse` dep), matching the light `ArxivApiClient`/`SemanticScholarClient` style. (3) Streaming failures cross the `Flow` boundary as `AiException(AppError)` (a `Flow` needs an in-band failure channel; collectors `catch` and map) — `AppResult` stays at non-streaming boundaries. (4) `AiKeyVault` is a **sibling** of `TokenVault` (separate prefs file `arxiver_ai_keys`, provider-keyed) rather than generalizing `TokenVault` — avoids touching the routine token path and its redaction tests. (5) **`EncryptedSharedPreferences` runs under Robolectric** — the vault round-trip is CI-tested, not deferred to device. (6) Pinned `claude-sonnet-4-6`; model selection is a later enhancement. (7) "What leaves the device" preview moved to **P2** (it gates paper content on the chat path; P1.1 only sends the user's own test ping). |
| 2026-06-14 | v2 mapped at phase level (phases P1–P5 + `docs/SPEC-AI-PROVIDERS.md`), subphases planned individually. **Phase numbering adopted:** `P<n>` › `P<n>.<m>` › `P<n>.<m><letter>`; v2 is the release goal, not a phase; shipped v1 phases keep historical labels. Standout pillar = **AI understanding**: a provider-agnostic AI platform (`:core:ai`) with **multi-provider BYOK** (Claude Messages API + Gemini Developer API over OkHttp — *not* Firebase AI Logic, which proxies a dev key not the end-user's) and **on-device/edge** inference (Gemma 4 E2B 0.84 GB Apache-2.0 via LiteRT-LM; optional system Gemini Nano via ML Kit/AICore) with device-capability tiering + graceful degradation. Build order: P1 platform (P1.1 cloud BYOK → P1.2 on-device) → P2 chat/RAG → P3/P4/P5. RAG retrieval stays on-device (reuse bge embeddings + `VectorIndex`); only retrieved chunks + question reach a cloud provider. |
| 2026-06-14 | CI flakiness root-caused & fixed: rare merge-commit failures (#42 release-variant, #46 debug-variant; never reproduced locally) were cross-class leakage of process-global singletons (WorkManager via `WorkManagerTestInitHelper`, the DataStore-by-name instance) — same-`@Config` Robolectric classes share one sandbox. Fix: `unitTests.all { setForkEvery(1) }` in `:app` (one JVM per test class). Slower app tests, but deterministic; doesn't mask real failures. |

| 2026-06-14 | Latent NPE fixed (found via M.4 tests): adding a paper to a collection/tag does not create a `library_entries` row, so `observeCollectionPapers`/`observeTagPapers` (LEFT JOIN) returned NULL `status` into the non-null `LibraryRow.status` → crash when viewing such a collection/tag. Fixed with `COALESCE(le.status,'to_read')` + `COALESCE(le.added_at,…)` in both queries (no schema change). LibraryDaoTest guards it |
| 2026-06-14 | Release minification disabled (`isMinifyEnabled`/`isShrinkResources` = false) after the second R8 obfuscation casualty (v1.1.2): Preferences DataStore's bundled protobuf-lite resolves generated fields by name via reflection, so even compat-mode renaming broke the onboarding write (`Field value_ ... not found`, caught by the v1.1.1 crash reporter). Since the signed APK can't be device-tested in CI, surgical keep rules just defer casualty #3 (Room/Retrofit/ONNX); for a single-user sideloaded app, shrinking buys ~nothing, so turning it off eliminates the whole bug class. Re-enabling shrinking (with audited keep rules + on-device smoke) deferred to the v2 backlog; protobuf keep rules landed now so that path is safe |
